<tr>
<td class="noprint" colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><img alt="" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" width="33"/> <i><a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Celta_de_Vigo_season" title="2016–17 Celta de Vigo season">Current season</a></i></td>

</table>
<p><b>Real Club Celta de Vigo</b> (<small>Galician pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Galician" title="Help:IPA for Galician">[reˈal ˈkluβ ˈθelta ðe ˈβiɣo]</a></span>; <i>Royal Club Celta de Vigo</i>), or simply <b>Celta Vigo</b> or sometimes just <b>Celta</b>, is a Spanish professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Vigo" title="Vigo">Vigo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, currently playing in the <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">Liga</a>. It was founded on 23 August 1923 following the merger of <a href="/wiki/Real_Vigo_Sporting" title="Real Vigo Sporting">Real Vigo Sporting</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Fortuna_Foot-ball_Club" title="Real Fortuna Foot-ball Club">Real Fortuna Foot-ball Club</a>. Nicknamed <i>Os Celestes</i> (The Sky Blues), they play in sky blue shirts and white shorts. The club's home stadium is <a href="/wiki/Bala%C3%ADdos" title="Balaídos">Balaídos</a>, which seats 29,000 spectators. Celta's name is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> who were once present in the region. Its main rival is fellow Galician club <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coruña">Deportivo de La Coruña</a>, with whom it contests the <a href="/wiki/Galician_derby" title="Galician derby">Galician derby</a>.</p>
<p>Celta have never won the league title nor <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey</a>, although it has reached the final three times in the latter. One of the team's best seasons was <a href="/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_La_Liga" title="1970–71 La Liga">1970–71</a>, when they finished unbeaten at home and were known as the "giant-killers". Celta came sixth that season and qualified for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> for the first time. More recently, the club finished in their best-ever position of fourth in <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_La_Liga" title="2002–03 La Liga">2002–03</a>, qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2003–04 UEFA Champions League">2003–04 UEFA Champions League</a>, where they were eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the Round of 16.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>R.C. Celta de Vigo was formed as a result of the ambition of Vigo's teams to achieve more at national level, where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_people" title="Basque people">Basque</a> sides had been their <i>bête noire</i> in the Spanish Championship. The idea was to merge both teams to create a more powerful team at national level. The standard-bearer of this movement was Manuel de Castro "Handicap", a sports writer for the <i><a href="/wiki/Faro_de_Vigo" title="Faro de Vigo">Faro de Vigo</a></i> who, from 1915, began to write in his articles about the need for a unitarian movement. The slogan of his movement was <i>"Todo por y para Vigo"</i> ("All for and to Vigo"), which eventually found support among the managers of <a href="/wiki/Real_Vigo_Sporting" title="Real Vigo Sporting">Real Vigo Sporting</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Club_Fortuna_de_Vigo" title="Real Club Fortuna de Vigo">Real Club Fortuna de Vigo</a>. It was backed unanimously when De Castro himself presented the motion at the assembly of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Football_Federation" title="Royal Spanish Football Federation">Royal Spanish Football Federation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> on 22 June 1923.</p>
<p>On 12 July 1923, at the annual general meetings (AGMs) of Vigo and Fortuna held at the Odeon Theatre and in the Hotel Moderno, respectively, the merger was approved. Thus the "Team of Galicia" was born, as it was dubbed. In the last AGM of Fortuna and Vigo to approve the formation of a new club held on 10 August 1923, the members decided upon the team's name. Various names suggested include "Real Unión de Vigo", "Club Galicia", "Real Atlántic", "Breogán" and "Real Club Olimpico". The latter name was popular, but they eventually decided on "Real Club Celta", an ethnic race linked to <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>). The first president of Celta was Manuel Bárcena de Andrés, the Count of Torre Cedeira. At this AGM, the squad was also decided, which numbered 64 players in total and included some notable players from both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Fortuna_Foot-ball_Club" title="Real Fortuna Foot-ball Club">Fortuna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real_Vigo_Sporting" title="Real Vigo Sporting">Vigo</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Goalkeepers</b>: Isidro, Lilo and Rubido</li>
<li><b>Defenders</b>: Otero, Pasarín, Juanito Clemente, Daniel y Kaíto</li>
<li><b>Midfielders</b>: Jacobo Torres, Balbino, Queralt, Hermida, Pombo, Cruces, Córdoba, Máximo y Bienvenido</li>
<li><b>Forwards</b>: Reigosa, Chiarroni, Posada, Polo, Correa, Gerardito, Ramón González, Caride, Pinilla, Salvador, Chicha, Miguelito y Casal, Park.</li>
<li><b>Manager</b>: <a href="/wiki/Francis_Cuggy" title="Francis Cuggy">Francis Cuggy</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="EuroCelta">EuroCelta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: EuroCelta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>1997 through to 2003 saw arguably the best results in Celta's history, this period They were dubbed "EuroCelta" by the Spanish press as a result of their European exploits, notable results included a 4-1 aggregate win against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liverpool_FC" title="Liverpool FC">Liverpool</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_UEFA_Cup" title="1998–99 UEFA Cup">1998–99 UEFA Cup</a>, a 4-0 second leg thumping of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juventus" title="Juventus">Juventus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Cup" title="1999–2000 UEFA Cup">1999–2000 UEFA Cup</a> and a 7-0 home win against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SL_Benfica" title="SL Benfica">SL Benfica</a> also in the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_UEFA_Cup" title="1999–2000 UEFA Cup">1999–2000 UEFA Cup</a>.</p>
<p>The club would qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2003–04 UEFA Champions League">2003–04 UEFA Champions League</a> eventually going out in the last 16 to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arsenal_FC" title="Arsenal FC">Arsenal</a> 5-2 on aggregate.</p>
<p>Key players during the period included <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Mostovoi" title="Alexander Mostovoi">Alexander Mostovoi</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valery_Karpin" title="Valery Karpin">Valery Karpin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haim_Revivo" title="Haim Revivo">Haim Revivo</a>, though the squad also relied upon other international players as well, such as goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Cavallero" title="Pablo Cavallero">Pablo Cavallero</a>; defender and future coach <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Berizzo" title="Eduardo Berizzo">Eduardo Berizzo</a>, midfielders <a href="/wiki/Claude_Mak%C3%A9l%C3%A9l%C3%A9" title="Claude Makélélé">Claude Makélélé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazinho" title="Mazinho">Mazinho</a>; winger <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_Adri%C3%A1n_L%C3%B3pez" title="Gustavo Adrián López">Gustavo López</a>; and strikers <a href="/wiki/Catanha" title="Catanha">Catanha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lyuboslav_Penev" title="Lyuboslav Penev">Luboslav Penev</a>, amongst others.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline">Decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por,_27_outubro_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="994" data-file-width="1200" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por%2C_27_outubro_2012.jpg/220px-508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por%2C_27_outubro_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por%2C_27_outubro_2012.jpg/330px-508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por%2C_27_outubro_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por%2C_27_outubro_2012.jpg/440px-508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por%2C_27_outubro_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:508cdc331d159-img_partido_Celta-D%C3%A9por,_27_outubro_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Celta playing local rivals <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coruña">Deportivo de La Coruña</a> on 27 October 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Celta had a dramatic reversal of fortune in 2003–04. In the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_La_Liga" title="2002–03 La Liga">previous season</a>, they finished fourth in the league, putting them in the third qualifying round of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>. Celta entered the group phase after eliminating <a href="/wiki/SK_Slavia_Prague" title="SK Slavia Prague">Slavia Prague</a>, and eventually reached the last 16 before being knocked out by <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>. However, their domestic form was disastrous, finishing second-to-last in La Liga, thus sealing their relegation to the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>. Although the squad was heavily dismantled following the demotion, Celta earned an immediate return to the top flight after finishing second in <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2004–05 Segunda División">2004–05</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_La_Liga" title="2005–06 La Liga">2005–06 season</a>, they finished sixth earning a return once more to the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Cup" title="2006–07 UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>. They made it to the last 16 in that competition as well before losing to German side <a href="/wiki/SV_Werder_Bremen" title="SV Werder Bremen">Werder Bremen</a>. The next year, <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_La_Liga" title="2006–07 La Liga">2006–07</a>, Celta finished in 18th and were once again relegated to the Segunda División. At the end of June 2007, Celta avoided going into administration. However, if an agreement was not put in place between the club and its creditors within three months, then courts would declare the liquidation of the club's assets.</p>
<p>Due to heavy debt, the club was forced to sell many players and make tremendous cuts in the club's finances. Since then, they have been relying mainly on the reserve team, combined with some inexpensive signings. During the first three seasons in the Segunda División, the club struggled to avoid further relegation, all amid fears of the club's complete disappearance. This was a period of high instability, with constant changes of managers and players. In the 2010–11 season, however, the signings of striker <a href="/wiki/David_Rodr%C3%ADguez_S%C3%A1nchez" title="David Rodríguez Sánchez">David Rodríguez</a>, winger <a href="/wiki/Enrique_de_Lucas" title="Enrique de Lucas">Enrique de Lucas</a> and manager <a href="/wiki/Paco_Herrera" title="Paco Herrera">Paco Herrera</a> turned the situation around. The club finished sixth after a fantastic season and qualified for promotion. Nevertheless, they were eliminated in the first knockout round by <a href="/wiki/Granada_CF" title="Granada CF">Granada</a> after a penalty shootout, the game having finished 1–1 in 90 minutes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_La_Liga">Return to La Liga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Return to La Liga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 3 June 2012, Celta returned to La Liga after a five-year absence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> In their first season back, they avoided relegation to the Segunda División on the final day after beating <a href="/wiki/RCD_Espanyol" title="RCD Espanyol">RCD Espanyol</a> 1–0 to ensure a 17th-place finish. On 8 June 2013, Celta announced they had signed former <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> and then-<a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona_B" title="FC Barcelona B">Barcelona B</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Luis_Enrique_(footballer)" title="Luis Enrique (footballer)">Luis Enrique</a> to lead the club for the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_La_Liga" title="2013–14 La Liga">2013–14 season</a>. Under Luis Enrique, Celta flourished, finishing ninth. After Luis Enrique's departure, his replacement, <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Berizzo" title="Eduardo Berizzo">Eduardo Berizzo</a>, led the team to eighth in La Liga during <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_La_Liga" title="2014–15 La Liga">2014–15</a>, and in the following season, Celta challenged the top teams during the autumn.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_La_Liga" title="2015–16 La Liga">2015–16</a> season still under the guidance of <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Berizzo" title="Eduardo Berizzo">Eduardo Berizzo</a> would see Celta's highest finish in ten years, finishing in Sixth position<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> subsequently earning a place in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2016–17 UEFA Europa League">2016–17 UEFA Europa League</a></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_identity">Club identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Club identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kit">Kit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Kit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbcaption">Celta Vigo's original home colours (1923).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Celta's original team strip consisted of a red shirt, black shorts and blue socks. This was later changed at an unknown date to the traditional sky blue and white strip, representative of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galician_flag" title="Galician flag">Galician flag</a>.</p>
<p>Celta have the longest-running sponsorship deal in Spanish football, and one of the longest-running sponsorships in Europe alongside German's <a href="/wiki/VfL_Wolfsburg" title="VfL Wolfsburg">Wolfsburg</a> with <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, Italian's <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> with <a href="/wiki/Pirelli" title="Pirelli">Pirelli</a> and Dutch's <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV Eindhoven</a> with <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a>. Going back to the <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_La_Liga" title="1985–86 La Liga">1985–86</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> season, <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn" title="Citroën">Citroën</a>, the biggest employer in Vigo and in all of Galicia, has been their official shirt sponsor. Their business deal with kit supplier, <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a>, was also one of the longest-running ones – Umbro's regional headquarters are based in nearby <a href="/wiki/Redondela" title="Redondela">Redondela</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crest">Crest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Crest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Like many other Galician clubs, such as <a href="/wiki/SD_Compostela" title="SD Compostela">Compostela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racing_de_Ferrol" title="Racing de Ferrol">Racing Ferrol</a>, the club badge is based on the red <a href="/wiki/Cross_of_Saint_James" title="Cross of Saint James">cross of Saint James</a>. On top of the cross sits a <a href="/wiki/Sky_blue" title="Sky blue">sky blue</a> shield with two letter "Cs" (Club Celta). In 1923, Celta became one of several Spanish football clubs that were granted patronage by the Spanish crown and thus entitled to use <i>Real</i> (Royal) in their names and the royal crown on their badge. This right was granted to Celta by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_XIII" title="Alfonso XIII">Alfonso XIII</a>, and the club subsequently became known as <i>Real Club Celta de Vigo</i>. During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Second_Republic" title="Spanish Second Republic">Spanish Second Republic</a> (1931–1936), the title <i>Real</i> was removed from the club's name and the royal crown was taken off the club crest; however, it was returned under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_State" title="Spanish State">Spanish State</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_records">Club records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Club records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 31 August 2015 <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Most league goals</b> – 107, <a href="/wiki/Hermidita" title="Hermidita">Hermidita</a> (1945–56)</li>
<li><b>Most Primera División league goals</b> – 104, <a href="/wiki/Hermidita" title="Hermidita">Hermidita</a> (1945–56)</li>
<li><b>Most goals in a season</b> – 69, (1998–99)</li>
<li><b>Most league appearances</b> – 432, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Manolo_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Alfonso&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Manolo Rodríguez Alfonso (page does not exist)">Manolo</a> (1966–82)</li>
<li><b>Current player with most league appearances</b> – 165, <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Mallo" title="Hugo Mallo">Hugo Mallo</a></li>
<li><b>Biggest win</b> and <b>biggest home win</b> – 10–1 (<i>v.</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gimn%C3%A0stic_Tarragona" title="Gimnàstic Tarragona">Gimnàstic</a>, 23 October 1949)</li>
<li><b>Biggest away win</b> – 1–6 (<i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao" title="Athletic Bilbao">Athletic Bilbao</a>, 24 March 2002)</li>
<li><b>Biggest defeat</b> and <b>biggest away defeat</b> – 10–0 (<i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao" title="Athletic Bilbao">Athletic Bilbao</a>, 11 January 1942)</li>
<li><b>Most Home points in a season</b> –</li>
<li><b>Most Away points in a season</b> – 18 (2006–07)</li>
<li><b>Record transfer fee paid</b> – €13.5 million, <a href="/wiki/Catanha" title="Catanha">Catanha</a> from <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="Málaga CF">Málaga</a> (summer of 2000)</li>
<li><b>Record transfer fee received</b> – €14 million, <a href="/wiki/Claude_Mak%C3%A9l%C3%A9l%C3%A9" title="Claude Makélélé">Claude Makélélé</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Madrid" title="Real Madrid">Real Madrid</a> (summer of 2000)</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Celta_Vigo_B">Celta Vigo B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Celta Vigo B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Celta_de_Vigo_B" title="Celta de Vigo B">Celta de Vigo B</a> is Celta's youth team. It was founded in 1996 and plays in the <i><a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n_B" title="Segunda División B">Segunda División B</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_titles">National titles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: National titles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a></b></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd><b>Winners (3):</b> <a href="/wiki/1935%E2%80%9336_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1935–36 Segunda División">1935–36</a>, <a href="/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1981–82 Segunda División">1981–82</a>, <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1991–92 Segunda División">1991–92</a></dd>
<dd><i>Runners-up (4):</i> <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1968–69 Segunda División">1968–69</a>, <a href="/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1975–76 Segunda División">1975–76</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2004–05 Segunda División">2004–05</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2011–12 Segunda División">2011–12</a></dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey</a></b></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd><i>Runners-up (3):</i> <a href="/wiki/1947%E2%80%9348_Copa_del_General%C3%ADsimo" title="1947–48 Copa del Generalísimo">1947–48</a>, <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Copa_del_Rey" title="1993–94 Copa del Rey">1993–94</a>, <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Copa_del_Rey" title="2000–01 Copa del Rey">2000–01</a></dd>
</dl>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual">Individual</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Celta_de_Vigo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Individual">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Pichichi_Trophy" title="Pichichi Trophy">Pichichi</a> (1)</b></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>1947–48 – <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Pahi%C3%B1o" title="Pahiño">Pahiño</a> (23 goals)</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Zamora_Trophy" title="Ricardo Zamora Trophy">Zamora</a> (3)</b></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dd>1992–93 – <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ca%C3%B1izares" title="Santiago Cañizares">Santiago Cañizares</a> (30 Goals/36 Games – Coef. 0.83)</dd>
<dd>2002–03 – <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina"><img alt="Argentina" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/23px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/35px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_Argentina.svg/46px-Flag_of_Argentina.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pablo_Oscar_Cavallero" title="Pablo Oscar Cavallero">Pablo Cavallero</a> (27 Goals/34 Games – Coef. 0.79)</dd>
<dd>2005–06 – <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Pinto_Colorado" title="José Manuel Pinto Colorado">José Manuel Pinto</a> (28 Goals/36 Games – Coef. 0.78)</dd>
</dl>

"Raining Champions". <i>Morbo: The Story of Spanish Football</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kings_Lynn" title="Kings Lynn">Kings Lynn</a>, England: <a href="/wiki/When_Saturday_Comes" title="When Saturday Comes">WSC Books</a>. pp. 165–181. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-9540134-6-8" title="Special:BookSources/0-9540134-6-8">0-9540134-6-8</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACelta+de+Vigo&amp;rft.atitle=Raining+Champions&amp;rft.aufirst=Phil&amp;rft.aulast=Ball&amp;rft.btitle=Morbo%3A+The+Story+of+Spanish+Football&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.isbn=0-9540134-6-8&amp;rft.pages=165-181&amp;rft.place=Kings+Lynn%2C+England&amp;rft.pub=WSC+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
